The C20s, producing <i>TPS-f</i> genes, were suggested to be eudicot specific because both rice and sorghum lack this subfamily<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Chen, F., Tholl, D., Bohlmann, J. &amp; Pichersky, E. The family of terpene synthases in plants: a mid-size family of genes for specialized metabolism that is highly diversified throughout the kingdom. Plant J. 66, 212–229 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d10343e2938">41</a></sup>. Our data clearly indicate that this subfamily was present in the last common ancestor of all angiosperms but was lost from the grass family (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#Tab1">1</a>). Massive diversification of the <i>TPS-a</i> and <i>TPS-b</i> subfamilies within the Lauraceae is consistent with a previous report that the main constituents of 58 essential oils produced in <i>Cinnamomum</i> leaves are C10s and C15s<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Cheng, S. S. et al. Chemical polymorphism and composition of leaf essential oils of Cinnamomum kanehirae using gas chromatography/mass spectrometry, cluster analysis, and principal component analysis. J. Wood Chem. Technol. 35, 207–219 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d10343e2955">43</a></sup>. These findings are in congruent with the fact that fruiting bodies of the SCT-specific parasitic fungus <i>Antrodia cinamomea</i> can produce 78 kinds of terpenoids, including 31 structure-different triterpenoids (C30s)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Geethangili, M. &amp; Tzeng, Y. M. Review of pharmacological effects of Antrodia camphorata and its bioactive compounds. Evid. Based Complement. Alternat. Med. 2011, 1–17 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d10343e2962">48</a></sup>, many of which are synthesized via the mevalonate pathway, as are C10s and C15s followed by cyclizing squalenes (C<sub>30</sub>H<sub>50</sub>) into the skeletons of C30s<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Lu, M. Y. J. et al. Genomic and transcriptomic analyses of the medicinal fungus Antrodia cinnamomea for its metabolite biosynthesis and sexual development. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 111, E4743–E4752 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d10343e2971">49</a></sup>. It is reasonable to suggest that this fungus obtained intermediate compounds through decomposing trunk matters from SCT.</p><p>The 101 Ck<i>TPS</i> genes identified in the SCT genome are unevenly distributed across the 12 chromosomal scaffolds and include gene clusters from multiple subfamilies (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">30</a>). In the <i>Drosophila melanogaster</i> genome, ‘tandem duplicate overactivity’ has been observed, with tandemly duplicated <i>Adh</i> genes showing 2.6-fold greater expression than single-copy <i>Adh</i> genes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Loehlin, D. W. &amp; Carroll, S. B. Expression of tandem gene duplicates is often greater than twofold. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 113, 5988–5992 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d10343e2994">50</a></sup>. These rearrangement events may have also contributed to diversification of TPS enzymes in the SCT lineage and subsequent clustering of genes associated with mass production of terpenoids.</p><p>In summary, the availability of the SCT genome establishes a valuable genomic foundation that will help to unravel the genetic diversity and evolution of other magnoliids, and to give a better understanding of flowering plant genome evolution and diversification. At the same time, the reference-quality SCT genome sequence will enable efforts to conserve genome-wide genetic diversity in this culturally and economically important broadleaved forest species.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec11" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec11-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec11">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec11-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Plant materials</h3><p>All plant materials used in this study were collected from a 12-year-old SCT growing in Ershui Township, Changhua County, Taiwan (23° 49′ 25.9″ N, 120° 36′ 41.2″ E) during April–July of 2014–2016. The tree was grown up from a seedling obtained from the Forestry Management Section, Department of Agriculture, Taoyuan City, Taiwan. The specimen (voucher number: Chaw 1501) was deposited in the Herbarium of Biodiversity Research Center, Academia Sinica, Taipei, Taiwan.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Genomic DNA extraction and sequencing</h3><p>We used a modified high-salt method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Sandbrink, J. M., Vellekoop, P., Vanham, R. &amp; Vanbrederode, J. A method for evolutionary studies on RFLP of chloroplast DNA, applicable to a range of plant-species. Biochem. Syst. Ecol. 17, 45–49 (1989)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3022">51</a></sup> to eliminate the high content of polysaccharides in SCT leaves, followed by total DNA extraction with a modified cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Doyle, J. J. &amp; Doyle, J. L. A rapid DNA isolation procedure for small quantities of fresh leaf tissue. Phytochem. Bull. 19, 11–15 (1987)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3026">52</a></sup>. Three approaches were employed in DNA sequencing. First, paired-end and mate-pair libraries were constructed using the Illumina TruSeq DNA HT Sample Prep Kit and Illumina Nextera Mate Pair Sample Prep Kit following the kit’s instructions, respectively. All obtained libraries were sequenced on an Illumina NextSeq 500 platform to generate ~278.8 Gb of raw data. Second, SMRT libraries were constructed using the PacBio 20-kb protocol (<a href="https://www.pacb.com/">https://www.pacb.com/</a>). After loading on SMRT cells (SMRT Cell 8Pac), these libraries were sequenced on a PacBio RS-II instrument using P6 polymerase and C4 sequencing reagent (Pacific Biosciences). Third, a Chicago and a Hi-C library were prepared by Dovetail Genomics (Santa Cruz) and sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq 2500 to generate 150-bp read pairs.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">RNA extraction and sequencing</h3><p>Opening flowers, flower buds (two stages), immature leaves, young leaves, mature leaves, young stems and fruits were collected from the same individual (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">1c</a>) and their total RNAs were extracted<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kolosova, N., Gorenstein, N., Kish, C. M. &amp; Dudareva, N. Regulation of circadian methyl benzoate emission in diurnally and nocturnally emitting plants. Plant Cell 13, 2333–2347 (2001)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3048">53</a></sup>. The extracted RNA was purified using poly-T oligo-attached magnetic beads. All transcriptome libraries were constructed using the Illumina TruSeq library Stranded mRNA Prep Kit and sequenced on an Illumina HiSeq 2000 platform. A summary of transcriptome data is shown in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">2</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Chromosome number assessment</h3><p>Root tips from cutting seedlings were used to examine the chromosome number based on Suen et al.’s method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Suen, D. F. et al. Assignment of DNA markers to Nicotiana sylvestris chromosomes using monosomic alien addition lines. Theor. Appl. Genet. 94, 331–337 (1997)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3063">54</a></sup>. The stained samples were observed under a Nikon Eclipse 90i microscope (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">1a</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Genome size estimation</h3><p>Fresh leaves of SCT were finely chopped with a new razor blade in 250 µl isolation buffer (200 mM Tris, 4 mM MgCl<sub>2</sub>-6H<sub>2</sub>O and 0.5% Triton X-100) and mixed well, following the protocol of Dolezel et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Dolezel, J., Greilhuber, J. &amp; Suda, J. Estimation of nuclear DNA content in plants using flow cytometry. Nat. Protoc. 2, 2233–2244 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3083">55</a></sup>. The mixture was filtered through a 40-μm nylon mesh, followed by incubation of the filtered suspensions with a DNA fluorochrome (50 μg ml<sup>−1</sup> propidium iodide containing RNase A). Samples were analysed on the MoFlo XDP Cell Sorter (Beckman Coulter Life Science) and the Attune NxT Flow Cytometer (Thermo Fisher Scientific) in the Institute of Plant and Microbial Biology Flow Cytometry Analysis and Sorting Services at Academia Sinica, Taipei, Taiwan. Two and one replicates were performed on the former and latter machines, respectively, using chicken erythrocyte (BioSure) as an internal reference (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">1b</a>). The 1 C genome size for SCT was estimated to be 781–890 Mb (Supplementary Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">1b</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">2</a>). Estimates of genome size from Illumina paired-end sequences were inferred using Genomescope<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Vurture, G. W. et al. GenomeScope: fast reference-free genome profiling from short reads. Bioinformatics 33, 2202–2204 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3099">56</a></sup> (version 1.0; based on k-mer 31).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">De novo assembly of SCT</h3><p>PacBio reads were assembled using the FALCON<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Chin, C. S. et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single-molecule real-time sequencing. Nat. Methods 13, 1050–1054 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3111">57</a></sup> (version 0.5.0) assembler. The consensus sequences of the assembly were further corrected using PacBio reads using Quiver<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Chin, C. S. et al. Nonhybrid, finished microbial genome assemblies from long-read SMRT sequencing data. Nat. Methods 10, 563–569 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3115">58</a></sup> and Illumina reads using Pilon<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS ONE 9, e112963 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3119">59</a></sup> (version 1.22). The PacBio assembly was scaffolded using the HiRISE scaffolder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Putnam, N. H. et al. Chromosome-scale shotgun assembly using an in vitro method for long-range linkage. Genome Res. 26, 342–350 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3123">60</a></sup> (version July2015_GR), and consensus sequences were further improved using Pilon with one iteration<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS ONE 9, e112963 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3127">59</a></sup>. The genome completeness was assessed using a plant data set of BUSCO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Simão, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210–3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3132">20</a></sup> (version 3.0.2). To identify putative telomeric repeats, the assembly was searched for high copy number repeats less than 10 bp using tandem repeat finder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573–580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3136">61</a></sup> (version 4.09; options: 2 7 7 80 10 50 500). The heptamer TTTAGGG was identified (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">6</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Gene predictions and functional annotation</h3><p>Transcriptome paired-end reads were aligned to the genome using STAR<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Dobin, A., Davis, C. &amp; Schlesinger, F. STAR: ultrafast universal RNA-seq aligner. Bioinformatics 29, 15–21 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3151">62</a></sup> (version 2.5.3a). Transcripts were identified using two approaches: (1) assembled de novo using Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Haas, B. J. et al. De novo transcript sequence reconstruction from RNA-seq using the Trinity platform for reference generation and analysis. Nat. Protoc. 8, 1494–1512 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3155">63</a></sup> (version 2.3.2) and (2) reconstructed using Stringtie<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Pertea, M. et al. StringTie enables improved reconstruction of a transcriptome from RNA-seq reads. Nat. Biotechnol. 33, 290–295 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3159">64</a></sup> (version 1.3.1c) as well as CLASS2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Song, L., Sabunciyan, S. &amp; Florea, L. CLASS2: accurate and efficient splice variant annotation from RNA-seq reads. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, e98 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3163">65</a></sup>) (version 2.1.7). Transcripts generated from Trinity were remapped to the reference using GMAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Wu, T. D. &amp; Watanabe, C. K. GMAP: a genomic mapping and alignment program for mRNA and EST sequences. Bioinformatics 21, 1859–1875 (2005)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3167">66</a></sup>. The three sets of transcripts were merged and filtered using MIKADO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Venturini, L., Caim, S., Kaithakottil, G. G., Mapleson, D. L. &amp; Swarbreck, D. Leveraging multiple transcriptome assembly methods for improved gene structure annotation. Gigascience 7, giy093 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3172">67</a></sup> (version 1.1). Proteomes from representative reference species (Uniprot plants; proteomes of <i>Amborella trichopoda</i> and <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i>) were downloaded from Phytozome (version 12.1; <a href="https://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/">https://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/</a>). The gene predictor Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Stanke, M., Tzvetkova, A. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS at EGASP: using EST, protein and genomic alignments for improved gene prediction in the human genome. Genome Biol. 7, S11 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3189">68</a></sup> (version 3.2.1) and SNAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Korf, I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinformatics 5, 59 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3193">69</a></sup> were trained either on the gene models predicted using BRAKER1 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Hoff, K. J., Lange, S., Lomsadze, A., Borodovsky, M. &amp; Stanke, M. BRAKER1: unsupervised RNA-seq-based genome annotation with GeneMark-ET and AUGUSTUS. Bioinformatics 32, 767–769 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3198">70</a></sup>) or MAKER2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Holt, C. &amp; Yandell, M. MAKER2: an annotation pipeline and genome-database management tool for second-generation genome projects. BMC Bioinformatics 12, 491 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3202">18</a></sup>) (version 2.31.9). The assembled transcripts, reference proteomes, BRAKER1 and the BUSCO predictions were combined as evidence hints for input of the MAKER2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Holt, C. &amp; Yandell, M. MAKER2: an annotation pipeline and genome-database management tool for second-generation genome projects. BMC Bioinformatics 12, 491 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3206">18</a></sup>) annotation pipeline. MAKER2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Holt, C. &amp; Yandell, M. MAKER2: an annotation pipeline and genome-database management tool for second-generation genome projects. BMC Bioinformatics 12, 491 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3210">18</a></sup>) invoked the two trained gene predictors to generate a final set of gene annotation. Amino acid sequences of the proteome were functionally annotated using Blast2GO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Conesa, A. et al. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics 21, 3674–3676 (2005)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3214">71</a></sup> and eggNOG-mapper<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Huerta-Cepas, J. et al. Fast genome-wide functional annotation through orthology assignment by eggNOG-Mapper. Mol. Biol. Evol. 34, 2115–2122 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3218">19</a></sup> (version 1.0.3). NUPTs of SCT were searched against its plastid genome (plastome; KR014245 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Wu, C. C., Ho, C. K. &amp; Chang, S. H. The complete chloroplast genome of Cinnamomum kanehirae Hayata (Lauraceae). Mitochondrial DNA A DNA Mapp. Seq. Anal. 27, 2681–2682 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3223">72</a></sup>)) using blastn (parameters were followed from Smith et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Smith, D. R., Crosby, K. &amp; Lee, R. W. Correlation between nuclear plastid DNA abundance and plastid number supports the limited transfer window hypothesis. Genome Biol. Evol. 3, 365–371 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3227">73</a></sup>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Analysis of genome heterozygosity</h3><p>Paired-end Illumina reads of SCT were aligned to reference using bwa mem<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3239">74</a></sup> (version 0.7.17-r1188). PCR duplicates were removed using SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Li, H. et al. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3243">75</a></sup> (version 1.8). Heterozygous biallelic SNPs were called using SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Li, H. et al. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3247">75</a></sup> and consensus sequences were generated using bcftools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Danecek, P. et al. The variant call format and VCFtools. Bioinformatics 27, 2156–2158 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3251">76</a></sup> (version 1.7). Depth of coverage and alternative allele frequency plots were conducted using R version 3.4.2. The consensus sequence was fed to the PSMC program<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Inference of human population history from individual whole-genome sequences. Nature 475, 493–496 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3255">23</a></sup> to infer past effective population size. All of the parameters used for the PSMC program were at default with the exception of -u 7.5 × 10<sup>−9</sup> taken from <i>A.</i> <i>thaliana</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Buschiazzo, E., Ritland, C., Bohlmann, J. &amp; Ritland, K. Slow but not low: genomic comparisons reveal slower evolutionary rate and higher dN/dS in conifers compared to angiosperms. BMC Evol. Biol. 12, 8 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3267">77</a></sup> and -g 20 taken from <i>Neolitsea sericea</i> (Lauraceae)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Cao, Y. N. et al. Inferring spatial patterns and drivers of population divergence of Neolitsea sericea (Lauraceae), based on molecular phylogeography and landscape genomics. Mol. Phylogenet. Evol. 126, 162–172 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3274">78</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Identification of repetitive elements</h3><p>Repetitive elements were first identified by modelling the repeats using RepeatModeler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Smit, A. &amp; Hubley, R. RepeatModeler Open-1.0 (Institute for Systems Biology, 2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3286">79</a></sup> and then searched and quantified repeats using RepeatMasker<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Smit, A., Hubley, R. &amp; Green, P. RepeatMasker Open-4.0 (Institute for Systems Biology, 2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3290">80</a></sup>. Repeat types modelled as ‘unknown’ by RepeatModeler were further annotated using TEclass<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Abrusan, G., Grundmann, N., DeMester, L. &amp; Makalowski, W. TEclass—a tool for automated classification of unknown eukaryotic transposable elements. Bioinformatics 25, 1329–1330 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3294">81</a></sup>. Tandem repeats were identified using Tandem Repeats Finder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573–580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3298">61</a></sup>. The proportions of different types of repeats were quantified by dissecting the 12 largest scaffolds into 100,000-bp chunks and calculating the total lengths and percentages of the repetitive elements within the chunks. LTR retrotransposons (LTR-RT) domains were extracted following Guan et al.’s method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Guan, R. et al. Draft genome of the living fossil Ginkgo biloba. Gigascience 5, 49 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3302">82</a></sup>. Briefly, a two-step procedure was applied on the genomes. The first was to find candidate LTR-RTs similar to known reverse transcriptase domains and the second was to identify other LTR-RTs using the candidates identified in the first step. The identified LTR-RT domains were integrated with those downloaded from the Ty1/Copia and Ty3/Gypsy trees of Guan et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Guan, R. et al. Draft genome of the living fossil Ginkgo biloba. Gigascience 5, 49 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3307">82</a></sup>. Trees were built by aligning the sequences using MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772–780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3311">83</a></sup> (version 7.310; --genafpair --ep 0) and applied FastTree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Price, M. N., Dehal, P. S. &amp; Arkin, A. P. FastTree 2—approximately maximum-likelihood trees for large alignments. PLoS ONE 5, e9490 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3315">84</a></sup> with the Jones, Taylor and Thornton (JTT) model on the aligned sequences, and were coloured using the APE package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Paradis, E., Claude, J. &amp; Strimmer, K. APE: analyses of phylogenetics and evolution in R language. Bioinformatics 20, 289–290 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3319">85</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Gene family or orthogroup inference and analysis of protein domains</h3><p>The amino acid and nucleotide sequences of 12 representative plant species were downloaded from various sources: <i>A.</i> <i>coerulea</i>, <i>A.</i> <i>thaliana</i>, <i>Daucus carota</i>, <i>Mimulus guttatus</i>, <i>M.</i> <i>acuminata</i>, <i>Oryza sativa japonica</i>, <i>Populus trichocarpa</i>, <i>Vitis vinifera</i> and <i>Zea mays</i> from Phytozome (version 12.1; <a href="https://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/">https://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/</a>), <i>Picea abies</i> from the Plant Genome Integrative Explorer Resource<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Sundell, D. et al. The plant genome integrative explorer resource: PlantGenIE.org. New Phytol. 208, 1149–1156 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3379">86</a></sup> (<a href="http://plantgenie.org/">http://plantgenie.org/</a>), <i>Ginkgo biloba</i> from GigaDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Sneddon, T. P., Li, P. &amp; Edmunds, S. C. GigaDB: announcing the GigaScience database. Gigascience 1, 11 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3394">87</a></sup> and <i>A.</i> <i>trichopoda</i> from Ensembl plants<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Bolser, D., Staines, D. M., Pritchard, E. &amp; Kersey, P. in Plant Bioinformatics: Methods and Protocols (ed. Edwards, D.) 115–140 (Springer, New York, 2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3404">88</a></sup> (release 39). Gene families or orthologous groups of these species and SCT were determined by OrthoFinder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Emms, D. M. &amp; Kelly, S. OrthoFinder: solving fundamental biases in whole genome comparisons dramatically improves orthogroup inference accuracy. Genome Biol. 16, 157 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3408">21</a></sup> (version 2.2.0). Pfams of each species were calculated from the Pfam website (version 31.0; <a href="https://pfam.xfam.org/">https://pfam.xfam.org/</a>). Pfam numbers of every species were transformed into z-scores. Significant expansions or reductions of Pfams in SCT were based on a z-score greater than 1.96 or less than −1.96, respectively. The significant Pfams were sorted by Pfam numbers (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">19</a>). Gene family expansion and loss were inferred using CAFE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="De Bie, T., Cristianini, N., Demuth, J. P. &amp; Hahn, M. W. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics 22, 1269–1271 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3423">89</a></sup> (version 4.1, with an input tree as the species tree inferred from the single-copy orthologues).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Phylogenetic analysis</h3><p>MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772–780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3436">83</a></sup> (version 7.271; option --maxiterate 1000) was used to align 13 sets of amino acid sequences of 211 single-copy orthologous groups. Each orthologous group alignment was used to compute a maximum likelihood phylogeny using RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML-VI-HPC: maximum likelihood-based phylogenetic analyses with thousands of taxa and mixed models. Bioinformatics 22, 2688–2690 (2006)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3440">27</a></sup> (version 8.2.11; options: -m PROTGAMMAILGF -f a) with 500 bootstrap replicates. The best phylogeny and bootstrap replicates for each gene were used to infer a consensus species tree using ASTRAL-III<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Mirarab, S. &amp; Warnow, T. ASTRAL-II: coalescent-based species tree estimation with many hundreds of taxa and thousands of genes. Bioinformatics 31, i44–i52 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3444">28</a></sup>. A maximum likelihood phylogeny was constructed with the concatenated amino acid alignments of the single-copy orthogroups (version 8.2.11; options: -m PROTGAMMAILGF -f a), also with 500 bootstrap replicates.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Estimation of divergence time</h3><p>Divergence time of each tree node was inferred using MCMCtree of the PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586–1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3456">30</a></sup> package (version 4.9g; options: correlated molecular clock, JC69 model and rest being default). The final species tree and the concatenated translated nucleotide alignments of 211 single-copy orthologues were used as input of MCMCtree. The phylogeny was calibrated using various fossil records or molecular divergence estimate by placing soft bounds at split node of:(1) <i>A.</i> <i>thaliana–</i><i>V.</i> <i>vinifera</i> (115–105 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Kumar, S., Stecher, G., Suleski, M. &amp; Hedges, S. B. TimeTree: a resource for timelines, timetrees, and divergence times. Mol. Biol. Evol. 34, 1812–1819 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3471">90</a></sup>, (2) <i>M.</i> <i>acuminata–Z.</i> <i>mays</i> (115–90 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Kumar, S., Stecher, G., Suleski, M. &amp; Hedges, S. B. TimeTree: a resource for timelines, timetrees, and divergence times. Mol. Biol. Evol. 34, 1812–1819 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3485">90</a></sup>, (3) Ranunculales (128.63–119.6 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Morris, J. L. et al. The timescale of early land plant evolution. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 115, E2274–E2283 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3489">32</a></sup>, (4) Angiospermae (247.2–125 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Morris, J. L. et al. The timescale of early land plant evolution. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 115, E2274–E2283 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3493">32</a></sup>, (5) Acrogymnospermae (365.629–308.14 Ma)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Morris, J. L. et al. The timescale of early land plant evolution. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 115, E2274–E2283 (2018)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3498">32</a></sup> and (6) a hard bound of 420 Ma of outgroup <i>Physcomitrella patens</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="Pryer, K. M. et al. Horsetails and ferns are a monophyletic group and the closest living relatives to seed plants. Nature 409, 618–622 (2001)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3504">91</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Analysis of genome synteny and WGD</h3><p>Dot plots between SCT and <i>A.</i> <i>trichopoda</i> assemblies were produced using SynMap from the Comparative Genomics Platform (Coge<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Lyons, E. et al. Finding and comparing syntenic regions among Arabidopsis and the outgroups papaya, poplar, and grape: CoGe with Rosids. Plant Physiol. 148, 1772–1781 (2008)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3522">92</a></sup>) to visualize the paleoploidy level of SCT. Synteny blocks within SCT and between <i>A.</i> <i>trichopoda</i> and <i>A.</i> <i>coerulea</i> were identified using DAGchainer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 93" title="Haas, B. J., Delcher, A. L., Wortman, J. R. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. DAGchainer: a tool for mining segmental genome duplications and synteny. Bioinformatics 20, 3643–3646 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3539">93</a></sup> (same parameters as Coge:<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Lyons, E. et al. Finding and comparing syntenic regions among Arabidopsis and the outgroups papaya, poplar, and grape: CoGe with Rosids. Plant Physiol. 148, 1772–1781 (2008)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3543">92</a></sup> -E 0.05 -D 20 -g 10 -A 5). Ks between syntenic group pairs were calculated using the DECIPHER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Wright, E. S. Using DECIPHER v2.0 to analyze big biological sequence data in R. R J. 8, 352–359 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3547">94</a></sup> package in R. Depth of the inferred syntenic blocks were calculated using Bedtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Quinlan, A. R. &amp; Hall, I. M. Bedtools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics 26, 841–842 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3551">95</a></sup>. Both the Ks distribution and the syntenic block depth were used to determine the paleopolyploidy level<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Ming, R. et al. The pineapple genome and the evolution of CAM photosynthesis. Nat. Genet. 47, 1435–1442 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3556">96</a></sup> of SCT. Using the quadruplicate or triplicate orthologues in the syntenic blocks as backbones, as well as <i>A.</i> <i>trichopoda</i> regions showing up to four syntenic regions, we identified the start and end coordinates of linkage clusters (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM1">Supplementary Note</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">
                           <i>R</i> genes</h3><p><i>R</i> genes were identified based on ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Lozano, R., Hamblin, M. T., Prochnik, S. &amp; Jannink, J. L. Identification and distribution of the NBS-LRR gene family in the Cassava genome. BMC Genomics 16, 360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3583">97</a></sup>. Briefly, the predicted genes of the 13 sampled species were searched for the Pfam NBS (NB-ARC) protein family (PF00931) using HMMER version 3.1b2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Eddy, S. R. Accelerated profile HMM searches. PLoS Comput. Biol. 7, e1002195 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3587">98</a></sup>) with an <i>e</i>-value cut-off of 1 × 10<sup>−5</sup>. Extracted sequences were then checked for protein domains using InterproScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Finn, R. D. et al. InterPro in 2017—beyond protein family and domain annotations. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D190–D199 (2017)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3596">99</a></sup> (version 5.19–58.0) to remove false-positive NB-ARC domain hits. The NBS domains of the genes that passed both HMMER and InterproScan were extracted according to the InterproScan annotation and aligned using MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772–780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3601">83</a></sup> (version 7.310; --genafpair --ep 0); the alignment was then input into FastTree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Price, M. N., Dehal, P. S. &amp; Arkin, A. P. FastTree 2—approximately maximum-likelihood trees for large alignments. PLoS ONE 5, e9490 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3605">84</a></sup> with the JTT model and visualized using EvolView<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="He, Z. et al. Evolviewv2: an online visualization and management tool for customized and annotated phylogenetic trees. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, W236–W241 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3609">100</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">
                           <i>TPS</i> genes</h3><p>In addition to the 13 species proteome data set used in this study, transcriptome data from one Chloranthaceae species, <i>Sarcandra glabra</i>, and two magnollids representatives, <i>P.</i> <i>americana</i> (avocado) and <i>S.</i> <i>henryi</i> (saruma), were downloaded from the 1KP transcriptome database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Matasci, N. et al. Data access for the 1,000 Plants (1KP) project. Gigascience 3, 17 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3641">29</a></sup>. Previously annotated <i>TPS</i> genes of four species: <i>A.</i> <i>thaliana</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Aubourg, S., Lecharny, A. &amp; Bohlmann, J. Genomic analysis of the terpenoid synthase (AtTPS) gene family of Arabidopsis thaliana. Mol. Genet. Genomics 267, 730–745 (2002)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3653">101</a></sup>, <i>O.</i> <i>sativa</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Chen, F., Tholl, D., Bohlmann, J. &amp; Pichersky, E. The family of terpene synthases in plants: a mid-size family of genes for specialized metabolism that is highly diversified throughout the kingdom. Plant J. 66, 212–229 (2011)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3663">41</a></sup>, <i>P.</i> <i>trichocarpa</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 102" title="Irmisch, S., Jiang, Y. F., Chen, F., Gershenzon, J. &amp; Kollner, T. G. Terpene synthases and their contribution to herbivore-induced volatile emission in western balsam poplar (Populus trichocarpa). BMC Plant Biol. 14, 270 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3672">102</a></sup> and <i>V.</i> <i>vinifera</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 103" title="Martin, D. M. et al. Functional annotation, genome organization and phylogeny of the grapevine (Vitis vinifera) terpene synthase gene family based on genome assembly, FLcDNA cloning, and enzyme assays. BMC Plant Biol. 10, 226 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3682">103</a></sup> were retrieved. For species without a priori <i>TPS</i> annotations, two Pfam domains: PF03936 and PF01397, were used to identify against the proteomes using HMMER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Wheeler, T. J. &amp; Eddy, S. R. nhmmer: DNA homology search with profile HMMs. Bioinformatics 29, 2487–2489 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3689">104</a></sup> (version 3.0; cut-off at <i>e</i> &lt; 10<sup>−5</sup>). Pseudogenes and sequence lengths shorter than 200 amino acids were excluded from further analysis. Putative or annotated protein sequences of TPS (<i>n</i> = 702) were aligned using MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772–780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3702">83</a></sup> (version 7.310 with default parameters) and manually adjusted using MEGA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 105" title="Kumar, S., Stecher, G. &amp; Tamura, K. MEGA7: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis version 7.0 for bigger datasets. Mol. Biol. Evol. 33, 1870–1874 (2016)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR105" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3706">105</a></sup> (version 7.0). The <i>TPS</i> gene tree was constructed using FastTree<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Price, M. N., Dehal, P. S. &amp; Arkin, A. P. FastTree 2—approximately maximum-likelihood trees for large alignments. PLoS ONE 5, e9490 (2010)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d10343e3713">84</a></sup> (version 2.1.0) with 1,000 bootstrap replicates. The subfamily <i>TPS-c</i> was designated as the outgroup. Branching nodes with bootstrap values of &lt;80% were treated as collapsed.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0337-0#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>All of the raw sequence reads used in this study have been deposited in NCBI under the BioProject accession number <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA477266">PRJNA477266</a>. The assembly of SCT is available under the accession number GCA_003546025.1.</p>

I.J.T. and H.-M.K. performed the assembly and annotation of the SCT genome. L.-Y.C. and Y.-W.W. carried out the repeat analysis. E.S. carried out analysis of plastid DNA. C.-S.W., L.-N.W., H.-T.Y., C.-Y.H. and S.-M.C. conducted the experiments. I.J.T., Y.-C.L., H.-M.K., C.-Y.I.L. and J.L.-M. carried out the comparative genomics analysis. Y.-W.W., M.-H.H., K.-P.W. and S.-M.C. analysed the <i>R</i> genes. H.-Y.W., S.-M.C., C.-Y.H. and Y.-W.W. analyszed the terpene gene families. I.J.T., S.-M.C., and J.L.-M. wrote the manuscript. S.-M.C. and I.J.T. supervised the study.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
